  49. I stopped using shampoo about 4 months ago. Initially, I would just rinse my hair, but I found it difficult to detangle my hair after rinsing it. I have hip-length hair that is very fine and I usually have to use a lot of conditioner (an entire handful) just to make my hair manageable enough to brush.<br /><br />I came across Renpure at a local drugstore (where it costs 11 dollars) and tried it out. It has a very thin texture and does not lather. The scent is pleasant. The bottle says to use 10+ pumps, but I find that I have to use 20 pumps or more because of how long my hair is. I put most of it onto my scalp and I massage it in. I add a splash of water and work it down to the ends of my hair. After I'm done with the rest of my shower, I rinse out the Renpure.<br /><br />Within a week of using Renpure, I noticed is that my hair seemed to be falling out more than usual. First, I thought it was postpartum hair loss. Then, after I did some research, I learned that many regular shampoos and conditioners contain binding agents that prevent detached hair strands from falling out, giving the illusion of more volume. In other words, even though most people lose about 100 strands of hair per day, many of those strands stay on your head attached to other strands of hair if you use volumizing products. Many people who stop using shampoo experience increased shedding because these 100 strands actually fall out instead of falling out and getting stuck to other strands.<br /><br />Several months in, I notice that I lose about 10-15 strands of hair each time I use Renpure, which still alarms me, but I suppose it's normal after all. My hair is softer and in better condition than ever before. It is so much easier to detangle, and I can go much longer in between &#34;washes&#34;.<br /><br />One last note: I have gone through about 8 or 9 bottles of Renpure, and 3 of them have had defective pumps. I was unable to get the pump to work. Not the end of the world, but it's an annoying manufacturing defect.manufacturing defect.

This cannot be overstated. This stuff is basically lights oils used to remove the dirt and heavier oils from your hair. I suggest getting in the shower and rinsing your hair thoroughly with just water to get off some surface sweat, dirt and oil. Then rub in about 10 pumps of this stuff (assuming shoulder length hair, increase or decrease if you need). Rub it in so it's even throughout your hair. Leave it in and continue your shower, not getting your head under the water so you don't wash it out. You should feel the minty tingle. When you're done with your body then start to rinse and rub your hair for longer than you think you need to. Keeping rinsing, keep rubbing. At this point apply conditioner (I use Renpure Amazing Miracle and they pair well together). If you rinsed well there shouldn't be any residue.<br /><br />The very first time I used it I was underwhelmed. But as my hair got used to it it got softer and started behaving a lot better. Try this twice or three times before you decide you hate it. Also, every once in a while I suggest cleaning your hair will a little bit of baking soda in water or apple cider vinegar in water to get rid of build-up.   211. I see a lot of negative reviews of this stuff on here and I think it's mostly because of the foreign concept of a cleansing conditioner. It's not going to foam up like a conventional shampoo because A, there's no SLS in it and B, it's more of the consistency of a conditioner. So just pretend like you're just going to use conditioner on your hair and you'll be fine.<br /><br />That being said, there are some tricks to getting the most out of this stuff. First, use waaaay more than the directions say to use, especially if you've got crazy long/thick/curly hair like I do. I work it through in sections, paying really good attention to the crown of my head because thats where I had trouble the first 1-2 times I used this. Massage the crap out of your scalp, and then comb the stuff all the way down to your ends. If you've got fuzzy ends like I tend to get, put some more on the ends. Leave it on for a few minutes, but seriously not a lifetime. Then rinse! It's really not rocket science.<br /><br />I'm not wild about the scent of this one, but it doesn't last too long like other shampoos so I didn't remove any stars for that. My method is as follows:<br />wet hair thoroughly - 2 minutes<br />start with a few pumps of product at a time, working from scalp to ends, and front to back (up to 15 pumps) - 3 minutes<br />scrub scalp with fingertips / nails as if I were a mother treating a lice infestation patient - up to 5 minutes<br />do all other shower stuff - ???<br />rinse well, shaking and scrubbing as needed - 2 minutes<br />soap down the backside (slick, sticky back does not equal clean feeling)<br />roughly towel dry, then wrap to absorb excess moisture, braid, get in bed<br /><br />This method leaves my hair clean, soft, and feeling healthy. I do have hair that tends to be a little dry, but I don't think there's any need for you to suffer and end up with grease-slicked hair with any of these products! :) So, here's what I do, and I've never had a problem with greasiness. I hope it helps! First, make sure your hair is soaking wet throughout. Also, you have to use a LOT of product. I use a palm-full and I have pretty much a pixie-ish cut with longer bangs and layers on top (although I am probably using too much!). Anyway, I rub the product together in my hands for a second and then rub/distribute it all throughout my hair. I stick my head under the shower water for like 1.3 seconds to add a bit of water, and then with my fingertips directly on my scalp I massage vigorously all over my head/hair. It does actually sort of lather when I do this, like sort of a foamy lather. Anyway, I do that first in the shower, then leave the \\"lather\\" on throughout the rest of my shower while I'm washing my face, shaving, etc.Right before I'm done with my shower routine and ready to rinse out my hair, I add a little bit of water again and re-lather, then rinse very, very well. I feel like all the foaming/massaging really helps in avoiding the greasiness that I think would be likely if you just slapped it on and then rinsed it out. I use this exact same routine no matter which cleansing conditioner I use and again, I've never had any greasy issues. Anyway, I hope that helps anyone who's having probs!

(When my hair was shorter I skipped this step; step 4 was enough to detangle. Now it needs more slip because it's so long.)<br />4) Mix together in my palms a bit more of the Suave Coconut and some Herbal Essences Set Me Up gel, then work that combo through sopping wet hair, raking out any remaining tangles or loose hairs.<br />5) (&#34;Baptismal rinse&#34;) Splash some more water over the top of my head, flip my head upside down, and splash some more over the back of my upside-down head, then turn off the water.<br />6) With my head still upside-down, scrunch out as much water as I can while disrupting the curl clumps as little as possible, then plop the whole mess of hair into a t-shirt and tie it up before standing up, so that the curls essentially sit on top of my head and set themselves while the t-shirt absorbs the excess water. I leave the t-shirt on my head while I get dressed, or if I'm showering at night I'll just sleep with it on. When I take it off I just shake out my still-wet-but-not-dripping-anymore hair and let it air dry the rest of the way.

It isn't terrible, just not quite what I'd hoped.<br /><br />That said, I can see why people may have encountered difficulties, especially if they're not used to washing with conditioner (co-washing) or if they followed the directions without knowing how to adapt them for their own hair needs. The directions are more like guidelines - the amount they say to use might be far too much for short, thin hair (like mine) or not nearly enough for longer thicker hair. Basically, you want your hair to feel like the product has worked its way through all of your hair. You don't want to massage it in the way you would shampoo - something like a wide-toothed comb, or just using your fingers, is a much better option. You have to make sure to very thoroughly rinse all of the product out of your hair. Yes, you can use some as a styling aid later, but if you don't completely clear out what you've used for cleaning, you may be leaving dirt and oil behind, which can make your hair feel sticky and gross.<br /><br />For myself, I always do one quick wash (work the conditioner through, then immediately rinse) followed by a second one where I let it sit in my hair for the recommended 3-5 minutes. My hair is on the fine side, and shoulder length, so I've found that 5-7 pumps is more than enough for each round.

  320. I have fragile, fine hair and have happily used Wen (all of the basic ones, as well as some of the special edition formulas) for over a year. I ordered the Renpure Coconut Crème Cowash through Amazon on a recommendation and found it to be MUCH more drying than any of the Wen cleansing conditioners. My hair felt like straw after using it, although the addition of a moisturizing styling product saved the day. I have decided to use this as a body wash instead, as it works well for that purpose.<br /><br />However, I received the Renpure Solutions Rosemary Mint cleansing conditioner as a gift and used it last night. Surprisingly, that product is far different from the Coconut Creme cleansing conditioner--my hair felt soft, shiny and clean afterward, and the results were exactly like what I'd get from any Wen product, for a much lower cost! I was so excited that I ordered another bottle, along with the Pomegranate (will review that formula after I try it).<br /><br />This experience has led me to wonder if the Coconut Crème product Amazon sells is a fake. I have noticed that the Rosemary Mint and Coconut Creme labels are slightly different and that the Coconut Crème product is made by &#34;Renpure,&#34; whereas the Rosemary Mint product label says &#34;Renpure Solutions&#34;. Just a thought. I've known Amazon to sell knock-offs before (Timex 1440 watches, specifically). So maybe that's the problem here. Not sure, but I am certain there is a vast difference between the Renpure Coconut Crème Cowash and the Renpure Solutions Rosemary Mint cleansing conditioner formulas.<br /><br />I hope this is helpful for anyone like me who needs a very gentle conditioning cleanser like Wen but would like to find a cheaper alternative.
